CHAPTER 1
PARKS AND RECREATION
SECTION:
11-101: Park Maintenance
11-102: Time Limit
11-103: Persons Subject To This Chapter
11-104: Alcoholic Beverages
11-105: Solicitors
11-106: Littering
11-107: Parks, Recreation And Tourism Board
11-108: Powers And Duties
11-109: Members To Serve Without Compensation
11-101: PARK MAINTENANCE:
All parks or recreational facilities within the corporate city limits are
maintained by the city. All rules and regulations governing the city parks and
other recreational facilities is the responsibility of the city council. (Ord.
206, 9-6-1977)
11-102: TIME LIMIT:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person to gather or remain in any of the
municipal parks later than the hour of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. until
sunrise the following day. This provision is not to be considered with regard
to organized parties or groups using the swimming pool or tennis facilities.
   B.   The city may at its discretion suspend the above referred to hours on
holidays and special occasions when organized celebrations are taking place.
However, the organizers of such groups or celebrations should notify the city
seven (7) days prior to such meeting. (Ord. 206, 9-6-1977)
11-103: PERSONS SUBJECT TO THIS CHAPTER:
Every person, group or organization which are residents of the city or guests
therein, shall come within the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 206, 9-6-1977)
11-104: ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES:
It is unlawful for any person whomsoever to sell or consume any type of
alcoholic beverage within any of the municipal parks or other recreational
facilities. Any person found guilty of the above offense, upon conviction,
shall be fined as provided in section
1-108 of this code.
   A.   Exception: Organized special events or festivals that have been
permitted, sponsored or otherwise approved by the city of Prague may allow for
the sale of wine and beer and consumption of those alcoholic beverages sold if
individual vendors that participate in the event obtain a special permit from
the city of Prague. Permit applications and other permit requirements may be
obtained from the city of Prague. Failure to comply with the permitting
application process or its regulations will result in a violation of this
section and a fine against any violator. Additionally, consumption of any
alcoholic beverage on the property of any municipal park or recreational
facility not purchased from a properly permitted vendor will result in a
violation of this section and a fine against any violator. (Ord. 428, 1-9-2012)
11-105: SOLICITORS:
It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to use any part or parcel
of any park or recreational facility of this city for the purpose of sale,
barter, or exchange at retail or wholesale, without first obtaining a peddler's
license as set forth in part 9, chapter 1 of this code. (Ord. 206, 9-6-1977)
11-106: LITTERING:
It is unlawful for any person to deposit paper, bottles, cans, or any other
type of refuse whatsoever upon any recreational facility or municipal park
within the city. Any person who violates this section is guilty of the offense
of littering and upon conviction shall be fined as provided in section
1-108 of this code. (Ord. 206, 9-6-1977)
11-107: PARKS, RECREATION AND TOURISM BOARD:
   A.   There is hereby established the board of parks, recreation and tourism
commissioners which shall consist of five (5) members to be appointed by the
city council. The members shall serve terms as follows: (Ord. 261, 5-10-1982;
amd. Ord. 419, 7-12-2010)
      1.   Members one, three and five shall serve terms of two (2) years and
until their successors are appointed and qualified; and
      2.   Members two and four shall serve terms of three (3) years and until
their successors are appointed and qualified.
   B.   The city council shall, at this time of appointment, designate the
member position held by each appointee. (Ord. 261, 5-10-1982)
11-108: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   The powers and duties of the parks, recreation and tourism board shall
be as provided by applicable state law or ordinances.
   B.   The parks, recreation and tourism board shall be involved in the
oversight of and development of activities that are held in the city parks, and
activities that promote recreation and tourism in the city.
   C.   The parks, recreation and tourism board shall serve as an advisory
board to the city council on matters dealing with the city parks, recreation
and tourism opportunities for the city of Prague. (Ord. 419, 7-12-2010)
11-109: MEMBERS TO SERVE WITHOUT COMPENSATION:
The members of the parks, recreation and tourism board shall serve without
compensation, except that actual and necessary expenses shall be allowed and
paid by the city council from any sum set apart for park purposes. (Prior code
§ 1-23; amd. Ord. 419, 7-12-2010)
CHAPTER 2
CEMETERY
SECTION:
11-201: Rules And Regulations
11-202: Use Of Lots
11-203: Perpetual Care
11-204: No Structures Contrary To These Rules
11-205: No Enclosure Or Fence
11-206: Owners To Plant No Shrubs
11-207: No Transfers Without Approval
11-208: Monuments
11-209: Consent To Interment
11-210: No Casket Or Container To Be Opened
11-211: Only One Interment To A Space
11-212: Disinterment In Municipal Cemetery
11-213: Space To Be Paid For Before Interment
11-214: Fees For Spaces And Grave Openings
11-215: All Charges To Be Paid In Advance (Rep. by Ord. 397, 5-8-2006)
11-216: City Not Liable
11-217: May Remove Flowers And Other Objects
11-218: Not Liable For Objects Stolen
11-219: Boring, Digging And Glass Jars
11-220: Hours
11-221: Penalty
11-222: Outer Containers
11-201: RULES AND REGULATIONS 1 :
The municipal cemetery is a tract of land located one and one- half (11/2)
miles east of the corporate limits on U.S. Highway 62 devoted to cemetery
purposes and maintained on the park or lawn plan providing for perpetual
maintenance as a municipal service. These rules are adopted for the purpose of
the protection of each lot owner in the enjoyment of all privileges usually
enjoyed in all modern cemeteries, with the least interference with equal
privileges due all other lot owners. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
 
Notes
1 1. 11 OS § 26-101 et seq.
11-202: USE OF LOTS:
No lot is used for any other purpose than the interment of bodies of persons.
(Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-203: PERPETUAL CARE:
All lots sold are subject to perpetual maintenance, and are also subject to all
reasonable rules and regulations now existing, or which may be hereafter
adopted to meet conditions hereafter arising. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-204: NO STRUCTURES CONTRARY TO THESE RULES:
Lot owners shall make no improvements or erect any monument, marker or
structure contrary to these rules, and should any monument, effigy, structure
or other object whatsoever, or any inscription be placed in or upon any lot,
monument or marker which the city deems to be offensive or injurious to the
appearance of the surrounding lots or grounds, the city shall have the right
and authority to enter upon such lot and remove such offensive object or
inscription. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-205: NO ENCLOSURE OR FENCE:
No enclosure of any kind, such as a fence, coping, curbing, hedge or ditch,
shall be permitted around any lot or place of interment. Corner markers will be
permitted when not over six inches (6") in diameter and sunk flush with the
ground. The top of any place of interment shall always remain on equal level
with the surface of the ground adjacent to it. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-206: OWNERS TO PLANT NO SHRUBS:
No trees, shrubbery or plants shall be set, planted, pruned or removed from any
lot, place or location without the consent of the city. The city, acting for
the best interest of the cemetery and all of its lot owners, shall have
authority to prune, remove, transplant, any tree, shrub, plant or flower when
it is deemed to be in the best interest of all owners in maintaining the
beautification of the municipal cemetery. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-207: NO TRANSFERS WITHOUT APPROVAL:
No owners of any lot in the municipal cemetery shall sell or transfer the same
or any interest therein except as permitted by the laws of the state and these
rules and regulations, and no such transfer shall be effective as to the
management of the cemetery, unless and until the same is approved by a person
duly authorized and such approval endorsed upon the conveyance in writing. This
is in order that the Municipal cemetery shall have a complete record of
ownership and of persons entitled to use the same. A fee of ten dollars
($10.00) shall be charged for each transfer. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-208: MONUMENTS:
A permit must be obtained from City Hall before setting any monument. All
foundations shall be prepared and installations made of all markers and
monuments at the Municipal cemetery at the expense of the lot owner in view of
perpetual maintenance. Such foundations to be the depth and character which the
City shall prescribe. All monuments must be set according to rules described in
permit. (Ord. 397, 5-8-2006)
11-209: CONSENT TO INTERMENT:
No interment will be permitted in any lot without the consent of the owner or
guardian, showing the exact location of the interment to be made and not then
unless a proper burial certificate or permit is furnished. At least twenty four
(24) hours' previous notice is required before any interment is made, except in
extreme emergencies. Adjustments in time and charges may be made. (Ord. 215, 3-
20-1978)
11-210: NO CASKET OR CONTAINER TO BE OPENED:
No casket or container of a deceased human body shall be opened by any person
within the confines of the Municipal cemetery without an order of a court of
competent jurisdiction, except when the last services are being had and then
only with the consent of the person having charge and authority to do so. (Ord.
215, 3-20-1978)
11-211: ONLY ONE INTERMENT TO A SPACE:
Only one interment is permitted in any adult interment space, except:
   A.   In the case of a mother and infant;
   B.   Two (2) infants;
   C.   Two (2) cremations;
   D.   One cremation may be additionally interred with one adult.
Interment spaces shall not be split to increase the lot size. (Ord. 479, 1-14-
2019)
11-212: DISINTERMENT IN MUNICIPAL CEMETERY:
No disinterment is made except by the employees of the City under the
supervision of proper authority and with the consent of the owner, based upon
an official permit therefor. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-213: SPACE TO BE PAID FOR BEFORE INTERMENT:
All charges for the purchase price of actual spaces for interment and all
interment and removal fees, or for foundation charges or other work or services
for which charges are made shall be paid in advance and before the services are
performed, unless arrangements for payment has been made through City Hall.
Should the interment be made upon the faith of an insufficient or forged check,
draft or other bill of exchange, so that such service is obtained by fraud,
then the City shall have the right to remove such body to a single interment
space apart from the lot where such interment was made. (Ord. 397, 5-8-2006)
11-214: FEES FOR SPACES AND GRAVE OPENINGS:
The following rates are hereby established with regard to charges per space,
charges for special area per space, grave openings, and weekend grave openings,
in the Municipal cemetery and are as follows:
A. Charge per space                                             $250.00
B. Special area per space                                       300.00
C. Grave opening (weekday)                                      200.00
D. Saturday morning opening                                     300.00
E. Saturday afternoon opening                                   400.00
F. Holiday                                                      400.00
G. Grave opening for cremations or infants (weekday)            125.00
H. Grave opening for cremations or infants (Saturday)           200.00
I. Monument permit fee for all monuments and markers except for 20.00
   veterans' markers
 
(Ord. 397, 5-8-2006)
11-215: ALL CHARGES TO BE PAID IN ADVANCE:
(Rep. by Ord. 397, 5-8-2006)
11-216: CITY NOT LIABLE:
So long as the City and its officers and agents act in good faith and upon
reasonable grounds in making interments, removals or disinterments, it shall
not be liable in damage on account of forgeries or frauds of others or mistakes
honestly made, but the City shall use all reasonable means at its command and
shall be permitted to correct any such mistakes so that any person or persons
affected thereby may not suffer loss by reason thereof. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-217: MAY REMOVE FLOWERS AND OTHER OBJECTS:
Flowers, blankets, designs and frames shall be removable from any place of
interment at any time at the discretion of the City. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-218: NOT LIABLE FOR OBJECTS STOLEN:
The City is not liable for the safekeeping of any flowers, blankets, design or
other object authorized to be placed on any lot or grave and the foregoing will
be placed at the sole risk and responsibility of the lot owner. (Ord. 215, 3-
20-1978)
11-219: BORING, DIGGING AND GLASS JARS:
No boring or digging is to be permitted in any place of interment or upon any
lot except for the purpose of interment or disinterment or for some reason of
maintenance or beautification by the City and no glass or metal jars, dishes,
objects or containers shall be placed in or upon any lot. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-220: HOURS:
The Municipal cemetery is open to the public from sunrise until sunset. All
persons must enter through the gates of the cemetery during these hours. All
vehicles must travel on existing roads in the cemetery, with the exception of
maintenance vehicles used for mowing, opening and closing graves and leveling
of gravesites. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-221: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any provisions of this chapter or any of the ordinances
or regulations adopted by reference herein is guilty of an offense and upon
conviction shall be fined as provided in section
1-108 of this Code. (Ord. 215, 3-20-1978)
11-222: OUTER CONTAINERS:
All interments must be made in outer receptacle which may consist of vaults or
boxes made of steel, fiberglass, concrete or other nonperishable material
approved in advance by the City. It shall be the responsibility of the parties
involved, excluding the City, to place such outer receptacle in the open grave.
(Ord. 397, 5-8-2006)
CHAPTER 3
LIBRARY DEPARTMENT BOARD
SECTION:
11-301: Library Department; Board; Librarian
11-301: LIBRARY DEPARTMENT; BOARD; LIBRARIAN 1 :
   A.   There is a library department, which is under the supervision and
control of a library board of five (5) members. The mayor shall nominate and
the city council approve board members. For the initial round of appointments,
the mayor shall nominate and the city council approve the members for terms of
five (5), four (4), three (3), two (2), and one years, such that one member's
term expires each year and each term shall expire on June 30 of the term's last
year. Thereafter, The mayor shall annually nominate and the city council
approve one member per year for a term of five (5) years, the terms to expire
on June 30 of the term's last year.
   B.   The mayor and members of the city council may remove members of the
library board when it is necessary for the good of the service. Each year, the
board shall elect a chairman and a vice chairman from its own membership, and a
secretary, who need not be a member of the board. The board shall determine the
time and place of its regular meetings. The city manager, the chairman, or any
three (3) members of the board may call special meetings of the board. The
members shall serve without compensation. The board shall supervise and control
the public libraries of the city, and shall recommend to the city manager the
hire or removal of the librarian and the employees of the department. The city
manager shall have the sole power to either hire or remove the librarian, who
shall be an officer of the city, and all the employees of the department. The
board shall adopt regulations for the administration of the libraries. The
librarian, subject to the authority of the library board, shall have
supervision and control of the public libraries and of all employees thereof.
(Ord. 449, 10-13-2014)

ARTICLE A. GENERAL PROVISIONS
11-401: DESIGNATION OF CITY OWNED LAKES AND RESERVOIRS:
The lake constructed by the City is hereby designated and named "Prague
Municipal Lake", hereinafter called "lake", and the police power of the City is
hereby extended to cover such lake. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-402: OPENING AND CLOSING HOURS:
The lake will be open for public use during the hours of five o'clock (5:00)
A.M. to ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. daily. The lake and adjoining property will
otherwise be closed at all other hours except to campers remaining overnight
pursuant to permit. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-403: WADING, SWIMMING IN LAKE; PENALTY FOR VIOLATION:
No person shall wade or swim in the lake except in areas so designated and
shall do so at their own risk. Violation of this clause will be a misdemeanor
subject to fine. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-404: THROWING UNSANITARY ITEMS IN LAKE PROHIBITED:
No person shall throw into or permit to enter the lake, or place, throw or
deposit upon the lands and premises surrounding such waters, any unused bait,
worms, flesh of animals or other matter subject to putrefaction, or any human
or animal excreta or any other unsanitary or unsightly thing. (Ord. 277, 4-8-
1985)
11-405: BURNING OF TRASH, BRUSH ON LAND AROUND LAKE:
   A.   No person shall burn any trash or refuse upon the property comprising
the lake and owned by the City unless it is burned in an incinerator or
container to be approved by the City.
   B.   No person shall burn grass, brush or other refuse upon the lake
property belonging to the City without first obtaining permission to do so from
the City. No person shall burn grass or other rubbish around any cabin site or
upon any property under lease by the City to such person without first
notifying the City of his intention to do so and obtaining permission for the
same from the City. Any person desiring to burn such grass or brush shall
notify the City of the same and it shall be the duty of the City Manager to
supervise such burning and no fire shall be started except under the
supervision of the City Manager. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-406: COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL OF GARBAGE AND REFUSE AROUND LAKE; PROVISION
FOR VIOLATION THEREOF:
   A.   No person shall throw or place garbage upon the ground or the property
comprising the lake, and all garbage or trash shall be placed in containers and
removed from the premises when the container becomes full.
   B.   The City or its agents and servants shall cause garbage cans to be
placed in all picnic grounds used by the public and all persons using such
picnic grounds shall place all garbage and refuse in such can, and the same
shall be removed and taken care of by the lake caretaker.
   C.   Any person in violation of this clause or who refuses or neglects to
comply therewith shall be subject to fine. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
ARTICLE B. BOATING REGULATIONS
11-410: LICENSE TO OPERATE BOATS:
No person shall operate any boat upon any of the water of the lake, or any
tributary or arm thereof, without first obtaining a license from the City
therefor, and then only in conformity with the provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 343, 10-18-1999)
11-411: FEES:
Any person may obtain a license for the use of a rowboat, sailboat or motorboat
upon the lake upon application to the City Clerk or such other person as may be
designated by the City Council to issue the same. There is a fee associated
with this activity that is subject to modification by the City Council through
resolution. The current fee schedule may be obtained from City Hall. (Ord. 460,
11-9-2015)
11-412: ISSUANCE; TERMS; CONDITIONS:
   A.   All licenses issued pursuant to this article shall bear the date of
issuance and the date of expiration. All annual licenses shall expire on
December 31 of each calendar year, and all daily licenses shall expire at
twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight on the date of issuance.
   B.   All licenses shall be issued on forms provided by the City Clerk and
approved by the City Council.
   C.   Each person holding a license for boating upon the lake shall have his
license therefor in his immediate possession when so boating and shall produce
the same for inspection upon demand of any officer, custodian, patrol officer
or representative of the City. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-413: NUMBERING OF BOATS; RENEWAL:
   A.   All boats for which a license has been issued to operate on the lake
shall be numbered in the order in which the license is granted with numbers
beginning at "one" and running numerically for the full number of boats for
which licenses have been issued.
   B.   Any person owning an annual boat license for any calendar year who
obtains a new annual license for the ensuing year on or before January 10 of
any calendar year may retain the same number on his boat as of the previous
year, but unless such new annual license is obtained on or before January 10,
such number shall be forfeited and a new number obtained. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-414: REVOCATION:
   A.   All licenses issued pursuant to this article shall be conditioned upon
the strict observance by the holders and users thereof of the terms of this
chapter and any other ordinances, rules or regulations promulgated by the City
Council for the protection of the lake from pollution or contamination, all
State sanitary laws and all State and Federal game and fish laws, while upon
such water or the premises occupied thereby.
   B.   A violation of such condition shall constitute a violation of this
chapter and the City Council upon conviction of any such holder or user of such
license of such violation, in addition to other penalties for violation of this
chapter, may revoke and cancel the license of such holder and such convicted
holder or user shall not be eligible for another license until the City Council
shall so order. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-415: RESTRICTIONS ON OPERATION AND USE OF BOATS GENERALLY:
   A.   No boat shall be operated or permitted to be used upon the lake unless
such boat is equipped with and contains at least one Coast Guard-approved life
preserver for each person in such boat.
   B.   No person under the age of sixteen (16) years shall row, sail or
operate any boat upon such lake unless accompanied by a person over the age of
twenty one (21).
   C.   All boats when not in use shall be fastened securely to the shore by
rope or chain.
   D.   No person operating any boat upon such lake shall throw into or permit
to enter such water any unused bait, worms, flesh of animals or other matter
subject to putrefaction, or any human or animal excreta or other debris or any
other unsanitary or unsightly thing.
   E.   No boat propelled by motor on the lake shall be operated at a speed
greater than that which leaves no visible wake. Boats under way shall whenever
practical avoid persons or other boats which may be fishing and shall further
reduce their speed when in proximity of such persons or boats so as to prevent
disturbance thereof.
   F.   No person or persons shall be permitted to sleep, live, camp or cook in
any boat operated upon the water of the lake. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
ARTICLE C. FISHING REGULATIONS
11-420: FISHING LICENSE REQUIRED; EXCEPTIONS:
No person shall fish in any of the waters of the lake, or in or upon any
tributary or arm of such lake, without first obtaining a license from the City
therefor and then only in conformity with the provisions of this chapter. (Ord.
277, 4-8-1985)
11-421: PERMANENT LICENSES FOR PERSONS OVER SIXTY FIVE OR PERSONS WHEELCHAIR-
CONFINED:
   A.   Except as provided in this section, all bona fide residents of the
State who have attained the age of sixty five (65) years, or who have not
reached their sixteenth birthday, or are wheelchair- confined shall not be
required to purchase a license under this article from the City to fish in the
lake.
   B.   Any such person over sixty five (65) years of age shall make
application to the City Clerk for a permanent license to fish in such lake and
upon furnishing to the City Clerk written evidence of the fact that he is over
sixty five (65) years of age, he shall be granted a permanent license to fish
in such lake.
   C.   Any such person, who is wheelchair-confined, shall make application to
the City Clerk for a permanent application to fish in such lake. Written
evidence may be requested; upon approval he shall be granted a permanent
license to fish in such lake. (Ord. 343, 10-18-1999)
11-422: FEES:
   A.   All bona fide residents of the State may obtain a permit to fish in the
lake upon application to the Office of the City Clerk or such other person
which may from time to time be designated by the City Council to issue the
same. There is a fee associated with this activity that is subject to
modification by the City Council through resolution. The current fee schedule
may be obtained from City Hall.
   B.   The issuance of such fishing permits shall only be made to persons
possessing a valid State fishing license. (Ord. 460, 11-9-2015)
11-423: ISSUANCE; TERMS AND CONDITIONS; RESTRICTION ON USE OF CERTAIN FISHING
DEVICES; PENALTIES:
   A.   All licenses issued pursuant to this article shall bear the date of
issuance and the date of expiration. All annual licenses shall expire December
31 of each calendar year, and all daily licenses shall expire at twelve o'clock
(12:00) midnight on the date of issuance.
   B.   All licenses shall be issued on forms provided by the City Clerk and
approved by the City Council and shall be nontransferable.
   C.   Each person holding a license for fishing upon the lake shall have his
license therefor in his immediate possession when so fishing and shall produce
the same for inspection upon demand of any officer, custodian, patrolman or
representative of the City. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-424: REVOCATION:
All licenses issued pursuant to this article shall be conditioned upon the
strict observance by the holders and users thereof of the terms of this chapter
and any other ordinances, rules or regulations promulgated by the City Council
for the protection of the lake from pollution or contamination, all State
sanitary laws and all State and Federal game and fish laws, while upon such
waters or the premises occupied thereby; and a violation of any such condition
shall constitute a violation of the terms of this chapter and the City Council
upon conviction of any such holder or user of such license of such violation,
in addition to other penalties for violation of this chapter, may revoke and
cancel the license of such holder and such convicted holder or user shall not
be eligible for another license until the City Council shall so order. (Ord.
277, 4-8-1985)
11-425: AUTHORITY FOR USE OF LAKE GRANTED UNDER FISHING LICENSES:
   A.   The issuance of a fishing license pursuant to this article shall
entitle the holder thereof to fish at such times and in such parts of the lake
as may be designated by the City Council from time to time, provided that such
person shall possess at such time a State fishing license.
   B.   The holder of a fishing license under this article may be accompanied
and joined in fishing by his children not over the age of sixteen (16) years
and such children shall not be required to have a fishing license, provided
that all fish caught or taken by such children when accompanied by their
parents shall be in conformity with the limit and length regulations herein
contained. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-426: RESTRICTIONS UPON KIND AND AMOUNT OF FISH TAKEN:
   A.   No person shall take from the waters of the lake any of the following:
      1.   Largemouth or smallmouth bass under fourteen inches (14") in length;
or
      2.   Channel cat and blue cat under ten inches (10") in length.
   B.   All of the fish listed in subsection A of this section are hereby
declared to be game fish within the purview of this section, and no person
fishing under one license shall catch or retain more than fifteen (15) such
fish in one day and under no circumstances shall such maximum number of game
fish include more than five (5) bass.
   C.   No person having a license to fish in the lake shall at any time or in
any manner take from the waters of such lake any fish by means of trotlines,
throwlines, limblines, juglines, nets or traps which are strictly prohibited.
   D.   Any person violating this subsection upon conviction thereof shall
forfeit his license to fish in such lake and be subject to fine for each fish
so caught, and each fish so caught is hereby declared to be a separate and
distinct offense for the purpose of conviction thereof. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-427: RESTRICTIONS ON USE OF CERTAIN BAIT:
No game fish as defined by the laws of the State or this chapter, and no carp
or buffalo, shall be used as bait to fish in the lake and no person shall turn
loose any minnows or other bait fish in such waters. No person shall keep,
place or maintain in such waters any live box or other receptacle for keeping
minnows or other fish alive, except while actually fishing. (Ord. 277, 4-8-
1985)
ARTICLE D. HUNTING REGULATIONS
11-430: HUNTING LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall hunt or shoot upon any waters of the lake or in any tributary
or arm thereof, or on the lands owned and controlled by the City surrounding
such waters, without first obtaining a license from the City therefor and then
only in conformity with the provisions of this article. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-431: PERMANENT LICENSES FOR RESIDENTS SIXTY FIVE YEARS OF AGE OR OVER;
PERSONS UNDER SIXTEEN YEARS OF AGE PROHIBITED:
   A.   Except as provided in this section, all bona fide residents of the
State who have attained the age of sixty five (65) years shall not be required
to purchase a license under this article from the City to hunt in the lake.
   B.   Any such person shall make application to the City Clerk for a
permanent license to hunt in such lake and upon furnishing to the City Clerk
written evidence of the fact that he is over sixty five (65) years of age, he
shall be granted a permanent license to hunt in such lake.
   C.   Persons under sixteen (16) years of age are prohibited from hunting on
the lake or its surrounding lands unless accompanied by a licensed adult. (Ord.
277, 4-8-1985)
11-432: FEES:
   A.   Any bona fide resident of the State may obtain a license to hunt upon
the waters and lands of the lake upon application to the Office of the City
Clerk or such other person which may from time to time be designated by the
City Council to issue the same. There is a fee associated with this activity
that is subject to modification by the City Council through resolution. The
current fee schedule may be obtained from City Hall.
   B.   The issuance of such hunting license shall only be made to persons
possessing a valid State hunting license with all required stamps affixed
thereto. (Ord. 460, 11-9-2015)
11-433: ISSUANCE; TERMS; CONDITIONS:
   A.   All licenses issued pursuant to this article shall bear the date of
issuance and the date of expiration. All annual licenses shall expire December
31 of each calendar year, and all daily licenses shall expire at twelve o'clock
(12:00) midnight on the date of issuance.
   B.   All licenses shall be issued on forms provided by the City Clerk and
approved by the City Council and shall be nontransferable.
   C.   Each person holding a license for hunting upon the lake shall have his
license therefor in his immediate possession when so hunting and shall produce
the same for inspection upon demand of any officer, custodian, patrolman or
representative of the City. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-434: REVOCATION:
   A.   All licenses issued pursuant to this article shall be conditioned upon
the strict observance by the holders and users thereof of the terms of this
chapter and any other ordinances, rules or regulations promulgated by the City
Council for the protection of the lake from pollution or contamination, all
State sanitary laws and all State and Federal game and fish laws, pertaining to
hours of hunting and daily bag limits, while upon such waters or the premises
occupied thereby.
   B.   A violation of any such condition shall constitute a violation of the
terms of this chapter and the City Council upon conviction of any such holder
or user of such license of such violation, in addition to other penalties for
violation of this chapter, may revoke and cancel the license of such holder,
and such convicted holder or user shall not be eligible for another license
until the City Council shall so order. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-435: TYPES OF HUNTING PERMITTED AND PROHIBITED:
Hunting on the lake is restricted to the hunting and taking of migratory fowl
only as defined by the laws of the United States and the State. All other types
of hunting for upland game or birds is prohibited. Bow hunting of any type for
game or fish is prohibited. Rifled guns or caliber guns are prohibited and all
shotguns used shall be plugged as shall be required by State or Federal law.
(Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-436: BLINDS FOR WATERFOWL HUNTING PERMITTED; FEES:
   A.   Persons holding valid licenses to hunt upon the waters and surrounding
lands of the lake may construct blinds for their use in such areas as are from
time to time approved by the City Council, provided, however, no person shall
construct such a waterfowl blind within three hundred (300) yards of any public
camping or picnic ground nor within three hundred (300) yards of another blind.
   B.   Any person so constructing such a blind shall first be required to put
up a deposit with the City Clerk in a sum of fifty dollars ($50.00) and
designate the area where the blind is to be built. At the end of each season or
seasons and upon compliance with the provisions of this section the deposit
shall be returned to the depositor thereof and no fee shall be charged for the
building and maintaining of the blind or blinds during the hunting season or
seasons.
   C.   Location of all blinds shall be in designated areas only. The areas
shall be designated by a stake placed by the City. Stakes shall be assigned by
City officials on a first-come, first-serve basis after the fifty dollar
($50.00) deposit is made with the City. The building of such blinds shall be
the sole responsibility of the person building the same. At the close of
waterfowl hunting season any such person so building a blind shall be
responsible for tearing down and removing the same from the grounds of the lake
and failure to do so will result in the forfeiture of deposit herein required.
   D.   Blinds are limited in number to one per person or family. At no time
shall there be more than four (4) persons in a blind.
   E.   Pits for the hunting of geese or other migratory birds is hereby
prohibited. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985; amd. Ord. 284, 11-10-1986)
11-437: AUTHORITY GRANTED UNDER HUNTING LICENSES GENERALLY:
The issuance of a hunting license pursuant to this article shall entitle the
holder thereof to hunt at such times and in such parts of the lake, and land
owned or controlled by the City surrounding such lakes, as may be designated
from time to time by the City Council. Such person shall possess at such time a
State hunting license with all required stamps affixed thereto. (Ord. 277, 4-8-
1985)
11-438: PROHIBITIONS AND RESTRICTIONS ON HUNTING GENERALLY:
   A.   The holder of a hunting license under this article shall have the
privilege of hunting for and shooting upon the lake and the land surrounding
the same, any duck, geese and other waterfowl in such places and at such times
as the City Council shall from time to time direct. Such areas of such waters,
or the lands surrounding the same, as may at times be restricted against
hunting or shooting thereon shall be designated by signs thereon or adjacent
thereto.
   B.   Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, no holder of a hunting
license or any other person shall at any time hunt or shoot any game of any
kind upon such waters, or the land surrounding the same, except ducks, geese
and other waterfowl, and no holder of a hunting license or any other person
shall use, shoot or discharge upon such waters, or the lands surrounding the
same, any firearm other than a shotgun, and shot used with or fired from such
shotgun shall not be a size larger than number 2, and shall be steel shot only,
all lead shot being specifically prohibited. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
ARTICLE E. CAMPING
11-440: CAMPING PERMITTED; TYPES OF CAMPING; AREAS DESIGNATED:
   A.   Camping shall be permitted upon the grounds of the lake for a period of
not to exceed seven (7) days at any given period, in areas designated and set
aside for that purpose by the City Council and so marked, and upon the payment
of fees hereinafter fixed.
   B.   Camping in any form will be permitted, but where the same is by use of
a camping trailer, pickup camper or other type of vehicular or mobile homes,
the same shall be restricted to designated parking areas and at no time shall
they be permitted to be parked or used outside the areas.
   C.   Wilderness or remote camping will be permitted by tent or open camping
on land surrounding the lake and outside of designated camping areas except
during hunting season when the same shall be prohibited. (Ord. 343, 10-18-1999)
11-441: CAMPFIRES:
   A.   Campfires will be permitted in all designated camping areas, but where
available shall be limited to receptacles constructed for that purpose. In the
event no such receptacle is available a campfire of small size for the purpose
of cooking may be built after an appropriate place has been cleared and
prepared so as to prevent the surrounding grass, trees and shrubs from catching
fire therefrom.
   B.   Campfires in wilderness areas are to be built with extreme caution and
only when the same does not constitute a fire danger to the surrounding areas,
considering the weather, wind and other factors which might cause any such fire
to spread. Any such campfire shall only be built when the person or persons
building the same have used all reasonable means at hand to prepare an adequate
and safe fire site so as to prevent its escape to the surrounding areas.
   C.   No campfire of any type shall be built or used by persons under
eighteen (18) years of age unless accompanied by a responsible adult who shall
supervise the same. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-442: FEES:
   A.   Any person or group of persons may camp on the lands of the lake upon
making application for a permit therefor to the City Clerk or such other person
or persons as may be designated by the City Council to issue the same. There is
a fee associated with this activity that is subject to modification by the City
Council through resolution. The current fee schedule may be obtained from City
Hall.
   B.   Any such permit issued pursuant to this section shall be for a twenty
four (24) hour period unless otherwise specified, in which event the fees for
such permit shall be the daily rate times the number of days specified.
   C.   Permits for camping shall be issued on the basis of camping unit
regardless of the number of people involved, such as for each tent, camp
trailer or vehicle. (Ord. 460, 11-9-2015)
ARTICLE F. GENERAL PROVISIONS RELATING TO CAMPING, HUNTING, FISHING AND BOATING
11-450: WOODCUTTING PROHIBITED:
All woodcutting upon the premises of the lake by a person or persons using the
same pursuant to the provisions of this chapter is hereby prohibited except
persons desiring to build campfires which may use such downed and dead timber
as may be available. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-451: WATERSKIING PROHIBITED:
Waterskiing upon the waters of the lake shall be prohibited at all times. (Ord.
277, 4-8-1985)
11-452: PRIVATE BOAT DOCKS PROHIBITED:
No person, persons, individual, partnership, firm, association or corporation,
other than the City and its licensees, may build, construct or erect any boat
or fishing dock upon the lake. However, the City Council may, at such time as
it elects, license the building and maintaining of one or more public boat or
fishing docks on such terms and conditions as it deems appropriate, the same to
be done by contract authorized by the City Council. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-453: FRUIT AND NUT GATHERING:
The public shall be permitted to gather and harvest indigenous fruits and nuts
growing on the lands of the lake, provided that the same may be done without
the destruction of trees and plants producing the same. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
11-454: PERSONS UNDER THE INFLUENCE OF INTOXICATING LIQUOR OR DRUGS; PROVIDING
FOR A TEST THEREFOR AND PROVIDING PENALTY:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person to operate any boat on the lake, camp,
hunt, fish or otherwise use the facilities while under the influence of
intoxicating liquor or drugs as defined by the State Statutes as controlled
dangerous substances.
   B.   Any person using or permitted to use the lake hereby consents to taking
a breathalyzer test or blood or urine test given and applied in accordance with
the State's implied consent law which may be used in court against them and
should they refuse to do so, such refusal shall be competent evidence in court
and shall be the basis of revocation of any and all permits held by any such
person, and they shall no longer be permitted to use the lake or its property
pending further order of the City Council.
   C.   Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be guilty of
a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be punished as provided in section
1-108 of this Code. Fine and jail time or both shall be in addition to the
forfeiture of any permit or use of the lake. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
ARTICLE G. PENALTIES FOR VIOLATION
11-460: PENALTIES:
Each and every violation of any of the provisions contained in this chapter is
an offense against the City and upon conviction of such an offense the violator
will be punished by a fine as provided in section
1-108 of this Code. (Ord. 277, 4-8-1985)
ARTICLE H. PAVILION REGULATIONS
11-470: FEES:
   A.   Any person or group of persons may use the pavilions upon making
application for a permit therefor to the City Clerk or such other person or
persons as may be designated by the City Council to issue the same. There is a
fee associated with this activity that is subject to modification by the City
Council through resolution. The current fee schedule may be obtained from City
Hall. (Ord. 460, 11-9-2015)

CHAPTER 1
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS

   Article A. Planning Commission

12-107: Planning Commission; Powers And Duties

12-111: Additional Authority
   Article B. Board Of Adjustment
   (Reserved)
ARTICLE A. PLANNING COMMISSION
12-101: PLANNING COMMISSION CREATED 1 :
There is hereby created a Planning Commission for the City. This Commission
shall consist of five (5) citizens of the City. The members of the Commission
shall be nominated and appointed solely with reference to their fitness and
without reference to their party affiliation. They shall serve without pay.
(Prior Code, Sec. 16-1)
12-102: TERM OF OFFICE:
Members of the City Planning Commission shall hold office for a term of three
(3) years, with the exception in the first instance, two (2) shall be appointed
to serve a term of one year, two (2) for a term of two (2) years, and one for a
term of three (3) years, except when a vacancy occurs an appointment shall be
made to fill the unexpired term. (Prior Code, Sec. 6-2)
12-103: MAYOR TO BE EX OFFICIO MEMBER:
The Mayor of the City shall be ex officio member of the City Planning
Commission, but shall receive no compensation for such service. (Prior Code,
Sec. 16-3)
12-104: APPOINTMENT:
The Mayor of the City shall appoint members of the City Planning Commission,
subject to approval and confirmation by the City Council. (Prior Code, Sec. 16-
5)
12-105: OFFICERS TO BE ELECTED; REGULATIONS:
The members of the Planning Commission shall meet within two (2) weeks after
their appointment and confirmation and organize by election from their members
a chairman, vice chairman, and secretary, who shall serve for a period of one
year. They shall adopt from time to time such bylaws, rules, and regulations
and amendments thereto as may be necessary to effectuate the purpose of this
Chapter. (Prior Code, Sec. 16-6)
12-106: NO COMPENSATION; DUTIES; EMPLOYEES:
Members of the Planning Commission shall serve without pay. It is the duty of
such Commission to prepare, from time to time, plans for the systematic
development and betterment of the City as a place of residence or for business.
It shall have the power and authority to employ planners, engineers, attorneys,
clerks, and other help deemed necessary, subject to the approval of the City
Council. The salary and compensation of such employees shall be fixed by the
City Council, and shall be paid out of the City Treasury as officers and
employees. The necessary expenses incurred by the Commission shall be paid out
of the City Treasury as other legal expenses of the City government. (Prior
Code, Sec. 16-7)
12-107: PLANNING COMMISSION; POWERS AND DUTIES:
The City Planning Commission may consider and investigate any subject matter
tending to the development and betterment of the City and make recommendations
as it may deem advisable concerning the adoption thereof to the City Council,
and for any purpose make or cause to be made, surveys, maps or plans. Before
the final action shall be taken by the City Council in the location and design
of any public building, statue, memorial, park, boulevard, street and alley,
playgrounds, public grounds, bridge or change in the location of any street or
alley or the grade thereof, such questions shall be submitted to the City
Planning Commission for investigation and report. The Planning Commission may
prepare and recommend to the City Council the adoption of rules and regulations
governing the subdivisions of land within the corporate limits of the City. All
plans, plats or other portions of the same intended to be dedicated to public
or private use within the corporate limits of the City shall first be submitted
to the Planning Commission for its recommendation, approval, or rejection. The
disapproval of any such plan, plat or replat by the City Council shall be
deemed a refusal of the purported dedication shown thereon. (Prior Code, Sec.
16-8)
12-108: PLANNING COMMISSION TO ACT AS ZONING COMMISSION:
The City Planning Commission also shall act as the Zoning Commission and shall
have the power to prepare and recommend to the City Council zoning district
boundaries and appropriate regulations relating to the height, number of
stories, and size of buildings and other structures, the percentage of lot that
may be occupied, the size of yards, courts and other open spaces, the density
of population, the location and use of buildings, structures and land for
trade, industry, residences and other purposes. (Prior Code, Sec. 16-10)
12-109: UNIFORMITY OF REGULATIONS:
The Planning Commission may recommend the division of the City into districts
of such number, size and area as may be deemed best suited to carry out the
zoning purpose. All such regulations shall be uniform for each class or kind of
buildings throughout each district, but the regulations in one district may
differ from those in other districts. Nothing in this Section shall be
construed to apply to telephone exchange buildings. (Prior Code, Sec. 16-10)
12-110: COMPREHENSIVE PLAN; PURPOSE OF REGULATIONS AND MATTERS CONSIDERED:
Such regulations shall be made in accordance with a comprehensive plan and
designed to lessen congestion in the streets; to secure safety from fire,
panic, and other dangers; to promote health and the general welfare; to provide
adequate light and air; to prevent overcrowding of land; to avoid undue
concentration of population; to facilitate the adequate provisions of
transportation, water, sewerage, schools, parks and other public requirements.
Such regulations shall be made with reasonable consideration, among other
things, as to the character of the districts and its peculiar suitability for
particular uses, with a view to conserving the value of buildings and
encouraging the most appropriate use of land throughout the City. (Prior Code,
Sec. 16-11)
12-111: ADDITIONAL AUTHORITY:
The City Planning Commission shall have additional authority and responsibility
as the City Council shall from time to time prescribe. (Prior Code, Sec. 16-12)
