City Manager, subject, however, to the person, firm or corporation first
obtaining written permission from the primary tenant of the land immediately
adjacent to the space so desired. The permission so obtained shall be renewed
and filed with the City Manager at the time of renewal of any taxicab license.
(Prior Code, Sec. 21-15)
16-211: CHAUFFEUR'S LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall drive or operate a taxicab unless the person first obtains a
chauffeur's license from the State. (Prior Code, Sec. 21-16)
16-212: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The City Council, after opportunity for a public hearing, may revoke any
taxicab license whenever a violation of any provision of this Chapter is shown.
(Prior Code, Sec. 21-17)
16-213: LICENSE FEE TO BE IN LIEU OF OCCUPATION TAX:
The license fee herein provided for shall be in lieu of occupation license
taxes heretofore required by ordinance. Occupation tax licenses heretofore paid
for the current year shall be credited on license fee herein provided for.
(Prior Code, Sec. 21-18)
16-214: REGULAR PLACE OF BUSINESS, TELEPHONE:
Any person, firm or corporation obtaining a taxicab license as herein provided
for and doing intra-City business within the City shall be required to have a
regular place of business and to maintain a telephone at the place of business.
(Prior Code, Sec. 21-19)
16-215: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation who violates any provision of this Chapter is
guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be fined as provided in
Section
1-108 of this Code. (Prior Code, Sec. 21-20)
PART 17
UTILITIES
Utility Services In General   1
Water Department And Services   2
Sewer System And Services   3
Refuse Collection   4
Landfill Regulations   5
Electric Service   6
CHAPTER 1
UTILITY SERVICES IN GENERAL
SECTION:
17-101: Utility Fees And Billings In General
17-102: Failure To Pay Utility Bills; Penalty And Disconnection Of Service
17-103: Utility Taps And Connections; Fees; Utility Deposits
17-104: Other Utility Fees Or Charges
17-105: City Personnel May Inspect Private Premises
17-101: UTILITY FEES AND BILLINGS IN GENERAL:
All fees and charges in connection with any customer's use of the City's
sanitary sewer system, the City's water facility system, or the operation of
the City's collection and disposal of refuse and garbage are billed in
accordance with applicable rates set by the City Council. All fees and charges
owing for any of these utility services shall be billed on one monthly bill
submitted to the customer each month. The utility bills submitted under the
terms of this Section are payable on or before the past due date which is
printed on the bill. (1983 Code)
17-102: FAILURE TO PAY UTILITY BILLS; PENALTY AND DISCONNECTION OF SERVICE:
Upon failure of any customer to pay any part of a utility bill submitted by the
City for any utility services pursuant to Section
17-101 of this Chapter by the past due date which is printed on the bill, the
following actions and penalties may result: (1983 Code)
   A.   Due Date And Second Notice Mailing: Utility bills are due by five
o'clock (5:00) P.M. on the fifteenth of each month. Any account not paid by the
fifteenth will have a ten percent (10%) penalty assessed and those customers
will receive a second notice in the mail. Second notices will be mailed to all
customers with outstanding balances regardless of deferred payment
arrangements.
   B.   Deferred Payment Agreements:
      1.   Customers will be allowed three (3) deferred payment arrangements in
a calendar year. However, the deferral must be made prior to disconnect day.
      2.   No customer will be allowed to sign an agreement if their
outstanding balance is more than four hundred dollars ($400.00), without prior
approval from the City Clerk or City Manager.
      3.   Any customer not honoring their deferred payment arrangement will be
disconnected immediately without notice. (Res. 97-04, 4-24-1997)
   C.   Disconnect Procedures:
      1.   The authorized agents of the City may disconnect or discontinue any
or all utility services to the customer after mailing or posting written notice
to the customer of the intent of the City to disconnect or discontinue any or
all of the utility services. (1983 Code)
      2.   Disconnect procedures begin at eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. on the
twenty fifth of every month unless the twenty fifth falls on a weekend, in
which case it will be eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. of the following Monday.
      3.   As stated above, no deferred payment arrangements will be accepted
on disconnect day.
      4.   A fifteen dollar ($15.00) service charge will be assessed to all
customers appearing on the disconnect list regardless of if services have
actually been disconnected at time of payment of past due bill. If a customer
wishes to have service reconnected after office hours, an extra five dollar
($5.00) service charge, in addition to the above mentioned fifteen dollar
($15.00) service charge will be assessed and due before services are
reconnected. (Res. 97-04, 4-24-1997)
   D.   Reconnection: If any utility service is discontinued or disconnected
pursuant to this Section, the City, or its agents, shall not reconnect or
reestablish the service until the full amount of any outstanding utility
service bill is paid, plus the penalty provided in this Section, plus any
applicable charges or expenses in reconnecting or reestablishing the service.
(1983 Code)
   E.   Returned Checks: A fifteen dollar ($15.00) service charge will be
assessed for each returned check received by the City. Any customer having a
returned check will have twenty four (24) hours to pay for the check plus the
service charge with cash or a money order before services are disconnected. Any
customer who has had two (2) or more checks returned to the City will be put on
a cash or money order only basis. (Res. 97-04, 4-24-1997)
17-103: UTILITY TAPS AND CONNECTIONS; FEES; UTILITY DEPOSITS:
   A.   The City shall approve any request for a water tap and connection, a
sewer tap on an existing line or a sewer tap on a new line. Prior to granting
this approval, the customer shall have paid the connection or tap charge as
applicable and set by ordinance or resolution of the Council. The deposit shall
serve as a guarantee for the payment of charges for utility service and other
amounts owed to the City in connection with the utility service. It shall be
held in trust by the City. When a customer's utility service is disconnected,
the deposit or any part of such amount deposited which remains after all such
charges and amounts due the City have been satisfied, shall be returned to the
customer.
   B.   A fee for reconnection of utility service where the service has been
turned off or a meter has been disconnected by the City for any reason shall be
set by the City Council. For any reconnection of utility service the charge
shall be set by the City Council. (1983 Code)
17-104: OTHER UTILITY FEES OR CHARGES:
The City Council from time to time by ordinance or resolution has the power to
establish rates and charges governing all aspects of the City utility services,
including monthly service fees, connection fees and charges, and deposits.
(1983 Code)
17-105: CITY PERSONNEL MAY INSPECT PRIVATE PREMISES:
City personnel in the service of the City's utility systems may enter any
private premises served by the City water or other utility systems at any
reasonable time, and inspect the water pipes and fixtures on the premises.
(Prior Code, Sec. 18-26)
CHAPTER 2
WATER DEPARTMENT AND SERVICES
SECTION:
17-201: Water System As Public Utility
17-202: Water Rates
17-203: Application For Water Service
17-204: One Premises To A Tap, Subsidiary Connection And Cross-Connection
Prohibited
17-205: Turning On Water
17-206: Water May Be Cut Off
17-207: Water To Be Turned Back On Only By City Authority
17-208: Customers To Keep Service Pipes In Good Repair, Not To Waste Water
17-209: Water Shortages, Declaration Of Emergency
17-210: Restriction On Water Use In Emergency
17-211: Proclamation And Notice Of Emergency
17-212: Grievances With Water Restrictions
17-213: Penalties
17-201: WATER SYSTEM AS PUBLIC UTILITY:
The water system of the City is hereby declared to be a public utility and a
proper source of City revenues and expenditures for the upkeep and maintenance
of the water system. (Prior Code, Sec. 18-10)
17-202: WATER RATES:
The City Council shall from time to time by ordinance or resolution set or
amend the fees and charges for water use by customers of the City's water
system. A copy of the current fees or charges shall be kept on file in the City
Clerk's office. (Prior Code, Secs. 18-16, 18-17)
17-203: APPLICATION FOR WATER SERVICE:
Any person desiring to secure water from the City water system, shall make an
application therefor to the City Clerk on an application form to be provided by
the City Clerk. The applicant shall give such reasonable information as the
City Clerk may request. He shall state in the application that he will abide by
all ordinances, rules, and regulations governing the water system of the City.
(Prior Code, Sec. 18-11)
17-204: ONE PREMISES TO A TAP, SUBSIDIARY CONNECTION AND CROSS-CONNECTION
PROHIBITED:
Not more than one premises may be connected to any one tap. No customer shall
make or permit to be made any subsidiary connection of another's premises with
his water service. A cross-connection with another water supply shall not be
permitted. (Prior Code, Sec. 18-14)
17-205: TURNING ON WATER:
It is unlawful for any person to turn the water on to any premises from the
Municipal water system, except by permission of the Superintendent. Water shall
not be turned on until the plumbing has been installed and is in operation as
provided by ordinance and until any and all deposits and charges have been
paid. The Superintendent will see that the water is turned on when all
requirements for service have been complied with. (Prior Code, Sec. 18-21)
17-206: WATER MAY BE CUT OFF:
   A.   Water may be cut off and service discontinued for any user of water
from the Municipal water system for any of the following reasons:
      1.   Violation of any ordinance provision relating to the water system,
or violation of any ordinance provision or any provision of any code adopted by
reference relating to water and sanitary plumbing;
      2.   Any act or omission in regard to the water system or sanitary sewer
system, the use of water, or the disposal of liquid wastes, which jeopardizes
the public health or safety, creates a public nuisance, or interferes with the
rights of others; or
      3.   Failure to pay a water bill or other proper charge in connection
with the water system by the time when the bill becomes delinquent. (Prior
Code, Sec. 18-19)
17-207: WATER TO BE TURNED BACK ON ONLY BY CITY AUTHORITY:
When the water of any customer has been turned off by City personnel, it shall
not again be turned on except by permission of the City. (Prior Code, Sec. 18-
21)
17-208: CUSTOMERS TO KEEP SERVICE PIPES IN GOOD REPAIR, NOT TO WASTE WATER:
All customers using Municipal water shall keep their service pipes, stopcocks,
and other water apparatus in good repair and in proper operation, and shall not
unnecessarily waste water. (Prior Code, Sec. 18-22)
17-209: WATER SHORTAGES, DECLARATION OF EMERGENCY:
   A.   Whenever an emergency exists by reason of a shortage of water due to
inadequate supply, limited treatment or distribution capacity or failure of
equipment or material, the Mayor is hereby authorized to restrict or prohibit
the use of water from the City's water system.
   B.   An emergency exists whenever the Mayor reasonably determines that the
City's water system is unable or will within sixty (60) days become unable to
supply the full commercial and domestic needs of the users thereof, including
adequate fire protection. (1983 Code)
17-210: RESTRICTION ON WATER USE IN EMERGENCY:
   A.   Upon the determination that such an emergency exists the Mayor shall
issue a proclamation declaring the emergency and setting out with particularity
an order restricting use of water from the City system. The order may:
      1.   Restrict water usage during certain periods of the day or week or
according to any orderly and nondiscriminatory scheme; and
      2.   Prohibit usages not essential to public health and safety. The order
may be revised from time to time as the Mayor deems necessary.
   B.   A duly proclaimed emergency shall continue and the terms of the
proclamation shall be in force for thirty (30) days or until such time as the
Mayor shall cause to be published a proclamation that the emergency has ended,
whichever is shorter, unless the Board, by resolution approved by a majority of
all its members, votes to terminate the emergency and proclamation upon a
different date. (1983 Code)
17-211: PROCLAMATION AND NOTICE OF EMERGENCY:
   A.   The proclamation required by the preceding Section shall be published
in a newspaper of general circulation in the City or, if there is no such
newspaper in which the proclamation may be published within twenty four (24)
hours after the emergency arises, publication shall be by posting a copy of the
proclamation in ten (10) prominent places in the City. The emergency shall be
in full force and effect upon publication. Substantial compliance with this
Section is sufficient to effect the emergency.
   B.   Whenever a sudden or unexpected event so reduces the availability of
water or water pressure as to create an immediate threat to public health or
safety the notice of the proclamation may be given by any reasonable means,
including electronic means. The emergency shall be in full force and effect
upon such notice. However, if any means other than that required in subsection
A of this Section is used, the proclamation shall be republished in accordance
with subsection A of this Section within twenty four (24) hours of the first
notice. (1983 Code)
17-212: GRIEVANCES WITH WATER RESTRICTIONS:
Any person feeling aggrieved by a proclamation of the Mayor shall have the
right to present the matter to the next regular or special meeting of the City
Council or to any emergency session called to discuss the water emergency. The
Board may exempt such aggrieved person, wholly or in part, from compliance with
the proclamation order upon a showing that compliance creates an immediate
threat to the person's health or safety. The ruling of the Council by a
majority vote of all its members shall be final and binding as to the
continuance of any terms of the proclamation. Until and unless the action of
the Mayor is modified or revoked by action of the Council all water users shall
be bound by the proclamation. (1983 Code)
17-213: PENALTIES:
Any person who in any manner directly or indirectly violates or permits others
under his supervision, custody or control to violate any term of a duly
published proclamation shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. Any violation of the
provisions of the Mayor's proclamation or action of the Board shall be
punishable by a fine or imprisonment as provided in Section
1-108 of this Code. (1983 Code)

17-301: DECLARATION OF PUBLIC UTILITY:
The sanitary sewerage system of the City is hereby declared to be a public
utility, and a proper source of revenue for the upkeep and maintenance of the
system and for other purposes. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-302: TAPPING, CONNECTION CHARGES:
   A.   The charge for the tapping of and tying onto the sanitary sewer system
in the City and all that portion of the City hereinafter brought within the
corporate limits of the City by appropriate ordinance or resolution adopted
thereafter, shall be the sum of the costs of all labor and material.
   B.   The charges made by this Section shall be paid to the Clerk of the City
prior to the installation of such equipment and/or service. (Ord. 344, 11-8-
1999)
17-303: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this Chapter, certain terms and words are to be used and
interpreted as defined hereinafter:
BOD (BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND): The quantity of oxygen utilized in the
biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure in
five (5) days at twenty degrees centigrade (20°C), expressed in milligrams per
liter.
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes inside
the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five
feet (5') outside the inner face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to the public sewer or
other place of disposal.
CITY MANAGER: The City Manager or his authorized deputy, agent or
representative.
COMBINED SEWER: A sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage.
CUSTOMER: The owner of the property served by a water connection, or the
tenant, lessee, renter, establishment, institution, or occupant of such
property, or the person in or against whose name the water connection for such
property is listed on the books and records of the City and who is responsible
to the City for the payment of bills incurred for water furnished to the
property, and for use by such property of the sanitary sewerage system of the
City, either or both.
DOMESTIC WASTEWATER: The liquid wastes:
A. From the noncommercial preparation, cooking and handling of food; or
B. Containing human excrement and similar matter from the sanitary conveniences
of dwellings, commercial buildings, industrial facilities and institutions.
GARBAGE: Solid wastes from domestic and commercial preparation, cooking,
dispensing of food and from the handling, storage and sale of produce.
INDUSTRIAL SEWAGE: The liquid waste resulting from any process of industry,
manufacturing, trade or business including cooling water that is discharged to
the sanitary sewerage system.
INDUSTRIAL USER: Any nongovernmental user of publicly owned treatment works
identified in the "Standard Industrial Classification Manual", 1972 Office of
Management and Budget, as amended and supplemented under the following
divisions:
A. Division A, agriculture, forestry and fishing;
B. Division B, mining;
C. Division D, manufacturing;
D. Division E, transportation, communication, electric, gas and sanitary
services; and
E. Division I, services.
A user in the divisions listed may be excluded if it is determined that it will
introduce primarily segregated domestic wastes or wastes from sanitary
conveniences.
mg/l: Milligrams per liter.
MAY: "May" is permissive.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body
of surface or ground water.
NORMAL STRENGTH SEWAGE: Sewage discharged by a user into the sanitary sewers
and in which the average concentrations of total suspended solids (SS) is not
more than three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l) and biochemical oxygen
demand (BOD) is not more than three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l).
PERSON: An individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation or
group.
pH: The logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per
liter of solution.
PLUMBING INSPECTOR: A person designated by the City Manager to inspect work and
compliance with ordinances and other laws governing the installation and
operation of sewer, water and gas plumbing.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food that have been shredded to such a degree that all particles
will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") in any dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal
rights and is controlled by public authority.
SANITARY SEWAGE: The "domestic wastewater" as defined in this Section.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer which carries sewage and to which storm, surface and
ground waters are not intentionally admitted.
SANITARY SEWERAGE SYSTEM: Includes all sanitary sewer trunk lines, main lines,
submain lines, lateral lines, lift stations and sewage treatment plants, and
all sewer lines connected to the City's sewer lines or treatment plants,
whether owned by the City or not.
SEWAGE: A combination of the water-carried wastes from residents, business
buildings, institutions and industrial establishments, together with such
ground, surface and storm waters as may be present and includes the domestic
wastewater and industrial sewage in any combination.
SEWAGE WORKS: All facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of
sewage.
SEWER SERVICE RATE: The price charged per unit (mg/l, 1,000 gallons, pounds) of
waste discharged into the sanitary sewerage system of the City.
SHALL: "Shall" is mandatory.
SLUG: Any discharge of water, sewage or industrial waste which in concentration
of any given constituent or in quantity of flow exceeds for any period of
duration longer than fifteen (15) minutes, more than five (5) times the average
twenty four (24) hour concentration or flows during normal operation.
STORM DRAIN (Sometimes Read "Storm Sewer"): A sewer which carries storm and
surface waters and drainage, but excludes sewage and industrial wastes, other
than unpolluted cooling water.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of, or are in
suspension in water, sewage or other liquids, and which are removable by
laboratory filtering.
SYSTEM: Any arrangement of devices and structures used for treating sewage.
USER: A "customer", as above defined, whose property also discharges sewage
into the sanitary sewerage system of the City in any quantity.
USER CHARGE: The monthly charge fixed for the user based upon the volume and
strength of sewage determined to be discharged by the user into the sanitary
sewerage system of the City.
WATERCOURSE: A channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or
intermittently. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-304: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS REQUIRED:
It is unlawful for any person to place, deposit or permit to be deposited in
any unsanitary manner on public or private property within the City or in any
area under the jurisdiction of the City, any human or animal excrement, garbage
or other objectionable waste. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-305: UNLAWFUL DISCHARGES:
It is unlawful to discharge to any natural outlet within the City or in any
area under the jurisdiction of the City any sewage or other polluted waters
except where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with subsequent
provisions of this Chapter. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-306: PRIVIES, SEPTIC TANKS, DECLARED UNLAWFUL:
Except as hereinafter provided, it is unlawful to construct or maintain any
privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool or other facility intended or used
for the disposal of sewage. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-307: SANITARY FACILITIES WITHIN TWO HUNDRED FIFTY FEET OF SEWER:
The owner of all houses, buildings or properties used for human occupancy,
employment, recreation or other purposes situated within the City and abutting
on any street, alley or right of way in which there is now located or may in
the future be located a public sanitary sewer of the City is hereby required at
his expense to install suitable toilet facilities thereon, and to connect such
facilities directly with the proper public sewer in accordance with the
provisions of this Chapter within ninety (90) days after date of official
notice to do so, provided that the public sewer is within two hundred fifty
feet (250') of the property line. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-308: PRIVATE SEWAGE DISPOSAL:
Where a public sanitary sewer is not available under the provision of Section
17-307 of this Chapter, the building sewer shall be connected to a private
sewage disposal system complying with the provisions of this Chapter. (Ord.
257, 12-14-1981)
17-309: PERMIT REQUIRED BEFORE COMMENCING CONSTRUCTION:
Before commencement of construction of a private sewage disposal system the
owner shall first obtain a written permit signed by the County Health
Department. The application for such permit shall be made on a form furnished
by the Health Department which the applicant shall supplement by any plans,
specifications and other information as are deemed necessary by the Health
Department. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-310: PERMIT NOT EFFECTIVE UNTIL INSPECTION AND REQUIREMENTS ARE MET:
A permit for a private sewage disposal system shall not become effective until
the installation is completed to the satisfaction of the County Health
Department. Representatives shall be allowed to inspect the work at any stage
of construction and, in any event, the applicant for the permit shall notify
the Health Department when the work is ready for final inspection, and before
any underground portions are covered. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-311: OKLAHOMA STATE DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH:
The type, capacities, location and layout of a private sewage disposal system
shall comply with all recommendations of the State Department of Health. No
septic tank or cesspool shall be permitted to discharge to any natural outlet.
(Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-312: ABANDONING PRIVATE SEPTIC TANKS UPON CONNECTION:
At such time as a public sanitary sewer becomes available to a property served
by a private disposal system, as provided in Section
17-307 of this Chapter, a direct connection shall be made to the public sewer
in compliance with this Chapter, and any septic tanks, cesspools and similar
private sewage disposal facilities shall be abandoned and filled with suitable
material. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-313: OPERATION OF PRIVATE SEWAGE FACILITIES:
The owner shall operate and maintain the private sewage disposal facilities in
a sanitary manner at all times at no expense to the City. (Ord. 257, 12-14-
1981)
17-314: ADDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS MAY BE IMPOSED:
No statement contained in this Chapter shall be construed to interfere with any
additional requirements that may be imposed by the Health Officer. (Ord. 257,
12-14-1981)
17-315: FILLING PRIVATE SYSTEMS:
When a public sewer becomes available, the building sewer shall be connected to
the sewer and the private sewage disposal system shall be cleaned of sludge and
filled with clean bank-run gravel or dirt. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-316: UNAUTHORIZED CONNECTORS; PERMIT REQUIRED:
No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any connections with or opening
into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or appurtenance thereof without
first obtaining a written permit from the Plumbing Inspector. (Ord. 257, 12-14-
1981)
17-317: CLASSES OF SEWER PERMITS:
   A.   There shall be two (2) classes of building sewer permits as follows:
      1.   For residential and commercial service; and
      2.   For service to establishments producing industrial wastes.
   B.   In either case the owner or his agent shall make application on a
special form furnished by the City. The permit application shall be
supplemented by any plans, specifications or other information considered
pertinent in the judgment of the Plumbing Inspector. A permit and inspection
fee of five dollars ($5.00) for a residential, commercial or industrial
building sewer permit shall be paid to the City at the time the application is
filed. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-318: COSTS BORNE BY OWNER:
All costs and expense incident to the installation and connection of the
building sewer shall be borne by the owner. The owner shall indemnify the City
from any loss or damage that may directly or indirectly be occasioned by the
installation of the building sewer. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-319: SEPARATE AND INDEPENDENT SEWERS REQUIRED; EXCEPTION:
A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every building
except where one building stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and
no private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building
through an adjoining alley, court, yard or driveway, the building sewer from
the front building may be extended to the rear buildings and the whole
considered as one building sewer. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-320: USE OF OLD BUILDING SEWERS:
Old building sewers may be used in connection with new buildings only when they
are found, on examination and test by the Plumbing Inspector, to meet all
requirements of this Chapter. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-321: CONSTRUCTION SHALL CONFORM TO CODES:
The design, size, slope, alignment, materials of construction of a building
sewer and public sewer, and the methods to be used in excavating, placing of
the pipe, jointing, testing, and back-filling the trench shall all conform to
the Oklahoma State Department of Health standards and to the requirements of
the building and plumbing codes or other applicable rules and regulations of
the City. In the absence of code provisions or in amplification thereof, the
materials and procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the ASTM
and WPCF Manual of Practice No. 9 shall apply. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-322: SEWER ELEVATION:
Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the building at an
elevation below the basement floor. In all buildings in which any building
drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary sewage
carried by such building drain shall be lifted by an approved means and
discharged to the building sewer. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-323: DRAIN CONNECTIONS NOT TO BE MADE TO SEWER:
No person shall make connection of roof downspouts, exterior foundation drains,
areaway drains or other sources of surface runoff or ground water to a building
sewer or building drain which in turn is connected directly or indirectly to a
public sanitary sewer. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-324: SEWER CONNECTION TO MEET SPECIFICATIONS:
The design, construction, and connection of the building sewer to the public
sewer shall conform to the requirements of the Oklahoma State Department of
Health standards and to the building and plumbing codes or other applicable
rules and regulations of the City, or the procedures set forth in appropriate
specifications of the ASTM and the WPCF Manual of Practice No. 9. All such
connections shall be made gastight and watertight. Any deviation from the
prescribed procedures and materials must be approved by the Plumbing Inspector
before installation. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-325: INSPECTOR TO BE INFORMED WHEN SEWER IS READY FOR INSPECTION:
The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify one or more times per
year from intermediate users and two (2) or more times per year from major
users. The City may or may not give prior notice of its intent to collect a
sample(s). (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-326: SEWER EXCAVATION TO BE GUARDED:
All excavations for building sewer installation shall be adequately guarded
with barricades and lights so as to protect the public from hazard. Streets,
sidewalks, parkways and other public property disturbed in the course of the
work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the City. (Ord. 257, 12-14-
1981)
17-327: WATER DRAINAGE NOT TO BE DISCHARGED INTO SANITARY SEWER:
No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any storm water, surface
water, ground water, roof runoff or subsurface drainage to any sanitary sewer.
(Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-328: STORM WATER AND UNPOLLUTED DRAINAGE TO BE DISCHARGED INTO PROPER DRAIN:
Storm water and all other unpolluted drainage shall be discharged to such
sewers as are specifically designated as storm sewers, or to a natural outlet
approved by the City Manager. Industrial cooling water or unpolluted process
waters may be discharged, on approval of the City Manager, to a storm sewer or
natural outlet. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-329: USER CHARGES:
   A.   For the purpose of providing funds for the operation and maintenance of
the sanitary sewerage system and for other purposes as allowed by applicable
law, there is hereby fixed and established a system of user charges comprised
of base level charges, surcharges and other charges to be levied against each
respective user thereof. The base level charges are based on the costs of
operation and maintenance of the sanitary sewerage system including replacement
as well as the volume, strength, and delivery flow rate of the sewage. The
costs of treating the extraneous flows shall be included in the cost of
operation and maintenance and, as such, shall be apportioned among the users on
the same basis as the other operation and maintenance costs. The base level
charge will be a uniform rate per unit of volume. The surcharges will be
developed as necessary and levied as applicable against the dischargers of
excessive strength waste and/or toxic pollutants. The surcharge will be based
on the cost of treatment of these wastes. The other charges are not related to
the cost of operation and maintenance but are for other purposes as allowed by
applicable law. They are based on volume but the rate per unit of volume will
decrease as the total volume increases. The user charge is the sum of the
various charges. The City shall review the base level portion of the user
charges annually and revise it as necessary to reflect the actual sanitary
sewage operation, maintenance and replacement cost and to ensure appropriate
distribution of the cost among the users. The City shall maintain such records
as are necessary to document the adequacy and proportionality of the base level
portion of the user charges. The records shall be maintained as long as
required by all applicable rules and regulations. The users shall be notified,
no less than annually, in conjunction with a regular bill, of the rates and the
portion of the user charge attributable to wastewater treatment services.
   B.   The monthly volume of sewage discharged by each user shall be assumed
to be equal to the quantity of water metered to the user but, in the cases
where the volume cannot be reasonably determined from the water so metered, the
amount of sewage discharged into the City system shall be determined as
provided in Section
17-330 of this Chapter.
   C.   A surcharge system meeting EPA requirements will be developed if
industries with above normal strength wastes and/or wastes containing other
pollutants that may increase the cost of operation and maintenance desire to
use the sewage facilities.
   D.   The wastewater from any industry(ies) that desires to use the sewage
facilities will be analyzed to determine the need, if any, to apply a
surcharge. The analyses will be carried out in accordance with the procedures
described in Section
17-331 of this Chapter.
   E.   The City Council shall from time to time by ordinance or resolution set
or amend the fees and charges for sewer use by customers of the City's sewer
system. A copy of the current fees or charges shall be kept on file in the City
Clerk's office.
   F.   Except as herein otherwise expressly provided each person, firm,
corporation, association, institution, or establishment from whose property or
premises sewage is discharged into the sanitary sewage system of the City but
who is not a water customer of the City is hereby required to meter, at its
source, the quantity of water used with an appropriate meter to be approved by
the City and to pay a monthly user charge based upon the quantity of water thus
metered and the strength of sewage discharged, to be computed in like manner as
provided in the preceding subsections of this Section.
   G.   Each user of the sanitary sewerage system of the City, who is a water
customer of the City but who also obtains, uses or consumes water from any
source other than from the City is hereby required to meter, at such source,
the quantity used, with an appropriate meter to be approved by the City, and to
pay a monthly user charge based upon the total quantity of water metered and
the strength of sewage discharged, to be computed in like manner as provided in
the preceding subsections of this Section. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-330: CLASSIFICATION OF INDUSTRIAL USERS:
   A.   Classifications of industrial users are as follows:
      1.   Minor users are those whose industrial discharge meets all of the
following criteria:
         a.   Flow: The maximum hourly rate of discharge is defined to be one
thousand forty two (1,042) gallons or less; and
         b.   Hourly Discharge: The maximum hourly rate of discharge is defined
to be the arithmetical average of any four (4) consecutive hours during which
the greatest total flow occurs;
      2.   Intermediate users are those whose industrial discharge exceeds the
criteria for a minor user but does not exceed any of the following criteria:
         a.   Flow: The maximum hourly rate of discharge, as previously
defined, does not exceed two thousand (2,000) gallons; or
         b.   BOD And SS: The BOD and/or SS concentrations in the discharge do
not exceed one hundred percent (100%) of the values shown for normal strength
sewage in Section
17-303 of this Chapter more than ten percent (10%) of the time; and
      3.   Major users are those whose industrial waste discharge does not meet
the flow, BOD or SS criteria listed for minor or intermediate users. (Ord. 257,
12-14-1981)
17-331: MONITORING OF INDUSTRIAL USERS:
   A.   The BOD and SS concentrations in the discharge of "minor users" will
normally be determined from standard values for various industries established
by the City Manager. However, the City Manager will collect samples and may
monitor discharge rates on a random basis. The intermediate users are required
to cause a sample to be collected and analyzed at least one time during any
twelve (12) consecutive months. The major users are required to cause a sample
to be collected and analyzed at least one time per month.
   B.   The sample shall be made up of individual portions collected,
composited and analyzed so as to permit determination of the maximum hourly
discharge rates as previously defined. The analysis shall be determined and
certified by an independent testing laboratory employed by the user and
approved by the City Manager.
   C.   A report shall be prepared and submitted to the City Manager within
fifteen (15) working days after the sample is collected. The report shall be
signed and shall contain a statement assuring that the sample was collected and
composited in such a manner as to be representative of the maximum hourly
discharge rate. It shall also include the:
      1.   Starting and ending time of the sampling period;
      2.   Hourly rate of flow observed during the sampling period;
      3.   Concentrations of BOD and SS;
      4.   Total pounds of BOD and SS discharged during the sampling periods;
and
      5.   Concentrations of other pollutants listed on the user's current
industrial discharge permit.
All costs associated with collection, compositing, analysis and reporting of
these samples shall be borne by the user.
   D.   The sampling point(s) shall be located, installed and maintained by the
user so that any authorized representative of the City may readily and safely
obtain samples of the discharge during all hours when discharge occurs. The
City can be expected to collect a grab sample one or more times per year from
intermediate users and two (2) or more times per year from major users. The
City may or may not give prior notice of its intent to collect sample(s). (Ord.
257, 12-14-1981)
17-332: PERMITS FOR INDUSTRIAL USERS:
   A.   A user discharging industrial wastes into the sanitary sewerage system
prior to the effective date of this Chapter may continue without penalty so
long as he does not increase the quantity of the discharge without the prior
permission of the City Manager and has discharged the industrial waste at least
three (3) months prior to the effective date of this Chapter and applies for
and is granted a "permit to discharge" no later than one hundred twenty (120)
days after the effective date of this Chapter. Section
17-329 of this Chapter on user charges shall take precedence over any terms,
conditions of agreement, or contracts between the grantee, the City and any
users that are inconsistent. Upon application on forms provided by the City,
permit to discharge may be granted to users provided that the user:
      1.   Submits an application within forty five (45) days after the
effective date of this Chapter;
      2.   Secures approval by the City Manager of plans and specifications for
pretreatment facilities when required;
      3.   Has complied with all requirements, including, but not limited to:
         a.   Payment of charges;
         b.   Installation and operation of pretreatment facilities; and
         c.   Sampling and analysis to determine quantity and quality;
      4.   A person applying for a new discharge shall:
         a.   Meet all conditions of this Section except subsection A1;
         b.   Submit an application for discharge sixty (60) days or more prior
to the planned initiation of such discharge;
         c.   Secure a permit to discharge prior to discharging any wastes; and
         d.   Demonstrate compliance with applicable State and Federal
statutes, rules and regulations; and
      5.   Permits issued under this Section are issued subject to conditions
listed thereon and all other applicable local, State and Federal statutes,
rules and regulations. The permits are subject to revocation for noncompliance.
The permit conditions are subject to modification by the City Manager if such
modification is or becomes necessary to protect the sanitary sewerage system or
its proper functioning, or if such modification becomes necessary as a result
of requirements imposed by the State or Federal government. (Ord. 257, 12-14-
1981)
17-333: EXCEPTIONS AND APPEALS:
   A.   Any person, firm, or corporations, association, institution, or
establishment from whose property or premises sewage is discharged into the
sanitary sewerage system of the City where the charges, as determined in
accordance with the provisions of Section
17-329 of this Chapter, do not reasonably reflect the amount of sewage and
concentration of BOD and/or suspended solids discharged by the applicant into
the sanitary sewerage system, may apply in writing to the City Council to make
a survey of the special facts and conditions shown to exist by such
application. After considering such application and survey, the City Council
shall determine the amount of sewage and concentration of BOD and suspended
solids discharged by the applicant into the sanitary sewer system under the
special facts and conditions shown to exist so that the charges to the
applicant will be just, fair and equitable.
   B.   Each user of the sanitary sewerage system of the City whose property or
premises may be located outside the corporate limits of the City shall pay as a
sewer service charge a sum equal to one hundred fifty percent (150%) of the sum
computed under the provisions of Section
17-329 of this Chapter. The City does not obligate itself to furnish sanitary
sewer service to any persons whomsoever, but will furnish such service as is
reasonable within its financial ability to do. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-334: COLLECTIONS:
The sewer service charge for the use of the sanitary sewerage system shall be
billed to each user monthly, along with the bill for water and other services,
and the City Clerk is hereby directed not to accept payment of the bill for
water and other services unless such payment is accompanied with the sewer
service charge. The failure to pay the sewer service when due shall be cause
for discontinuing and disconnecting either the sewer connection, the water
connection, or the electrical connection, or either or all of the connections.
(Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-335: DISPOSITION OF FUNDS:
The funds derived from the sewer service charge shall be deposited in the
general revenues of the trustees of the Prague Public Works Authority to be
used for the upkeep, maintenance, extension and repair of the sanitary sewerage
system and such other uses as are required of the trustees by law and the
obligations incurred by them. Any excess base level revenues that are collected
from a class of users shall be applied to the costs of operation and
maintenance attributable to that class for the next year and the rate shall be
adjusted accordingly. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-336: DISCHARGE OF SUBSTANCES, MATERIALS, WATER OR WASTE TO SANITARY SEWER
PROHIBITED:
   A.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the
following described waters or wastes to any public sewers:
      1.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid or gas;
      2.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous solids, liquids
or gases in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with other
wastes, to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process or facility,
constitute a hazard in the receiving waters of sewage treatment plant effluent;
      3.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5, or causing the pH
of the sewage plant influent to rise above 9.5, or having any other corrosive
property capable of causing damage or hazard to processes, structures,
equipment and/or personnel of the sewage works;
      4.   Solid viscous or liquid substances in quantities or of such size as
to cause or be capable of causing obstruction to the flow of sewers or other
interference with the proper operation of the sewage works such as, but not
limited to, ashes, cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags,
feathers, tar, plastic, wood, unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure,
hair and fleshings, entrails, paper products such as dishes, cups or milk
containers, either whole or ground by garbage grinders, slops, chemical
residues, or bulk solids;
      5.   Any strong acid, iron pickling wastes or concentrated plating
solutions whether neutralized or not;
      6.   Any unusual volume of flow or concentration of wastes constituting
"slugs" as defined herein;
      7.   Any substance that may pass through the treatment plant without
being effectively treated or otherwise reduced to acceptable concentrations by
normal treatment methods such that the sewage treatment plant effluent cannot
meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction over the discharge
to the receiving waters;
      8.   Any waste containing rhenium, strontium or tellurium; and
      9.   Any waters or wastes containing substances in excess of the limits
established in Section
17-337 of this Chapter or that have been diluted solely for the purpose of
meeting any concentration limits listed or implied in this Section and Section
17-337 of this Chapter. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-337: LIMITATION ON DISCHARGE OF SUBSTANCES, MATERIALS, WATERS, OR WASTES TO
THE SANITARY SEWER:
   A.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the
following described substances, materials, waters or wastes in concentrations,
quantities or rates in excess of those listed except as hereinafter provided:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) or sixty five degrees centigrade (65°C), or
any substance which causes the temperature of the total sewage plant influent
to increase at a rate of ten degrees Fahrenheit (10°F) or more per hour or a
combined total increase of plant influent temperature to one hundred ten
degrees Fahrenheit (110°F);
      2.   Any water or waste containing fats, wax, grease or oil, whether
emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred milligrams per liter (100 mg/l) or
containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures
between thirty two degrees Fahrenheit (32°F) and one hundred fifty degrees
Fahrenheit (150°F) (0° and 65°C);
      3.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage shredder equipped with a motor of three-fourths
(3/4) horsepower (0.75 hp-metric) or greater is subject to review and approval
of the City Manager;
      4.   Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or
concentration as may exceed limits to be established by the City Manager on a
case-by-case basis in compliance with and after consultation with the
appropriate regulatory agencies;
      5.   Any substance with a BOD or suspended solids concentration in excess
of three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l) except that upon receipt of a
written application and establishment of appropriate charges the City Manager
may, if the sewage works has sufficient unused or uncommitted capacity,
authorize the discharge of wastes containing BOD and/or suspended solids
concentrations in excess of three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l) each;
      6.   Any waters or wastes with total dissolved solids concentrations
greater than three thousand milligrams per liter (3,000 mg/l) plus the
dissolved solids in the City water supply;
      7.   Any waters or wastes containing excessive discoloration or causing
excess discoloration of the effluent, including, but not limited to, dye wastes
and vegetable tanning solutions;
      8.   Any waters, wastes or other substances containing one or more of the
following constituents in excess of the concentrations listed:
 Average For 30 Consecutive Days (mg/l) Maximum For Any 1 Day (mg/l)
                     Average For 30 Consecutive Maximum For Any 1 Day (mg/l)
                      Days (mg/l)
Antimony              0.01

Boron                 1.0                         
Cadmium               0.5                        1.0
Chromium - hexavalent 1.0                         
Chromium - total      5.0                         
Copper                1.0                         
Cyanide               1.0                         
Fluoride              1.5                         
Lead                  0.4                        0.8
Mercury               0.002                       
Nickel                1.8                        3.6
Phenols               0.1                         
Silver                0.3                        1.0
Vanadium              10.0                        
Zinc                  5.0                         
 
      9.   Limitation on elements or compounds not listed will be established
and/or limitations for elements or compounds listed will be lowered if
necessary to ensure that the effluent of the wastewater treatment plant is in
full compliance with legal requirements of County, State or Federal regulatory
agencies. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-338: CITY MANAGER MAY REQUIRE SPECIAL HANDLING OF WASTE:
   A.   If any waters or wastes are discharged or are proposed to be discharged
to the public sewers, which waters contain the substances or possess the
characteristics enumerated in Sections
17-336 and
17-337 of this Chapter, and which in the judgment of the City Manager may have
a deleterious effect upon the sewage works, processes, equipment or receiving
waters, or which otherwise create a hazard to life or constitute a public
nuisance, the City Manager may:
      1.   Reject the wastes;
      2.   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to the
public sewers;
      3.   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; and/or
      4.   Require payment to cover the added cost of handling and treating the
wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charges under the provisions of
Section
17-343 of this Chapter.
   B.   If the City Manager permits the pretreatment or equalization of waste
flows, the design and installation of the plant and equipment is subject to the
review and approval of the City Manager, and subject to the requirements of all
applicable codes, ordinances and laws. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-339: CITY MANAGER MAY REQUIRE GREASE, OIL INTERCEPTORS:
Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the opinion of the
City Manager they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes
containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand or other
harmful ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be required for
private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall be of a type
and capacity approved by the City Manager and shall be located as to be readily
and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-340: SPECIAL EQUIPMENT TO BE MAINTAINED BY OWNER:
Where preliminary treatment or flow-equalizing facilities are provided for any
waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in satisfactory and
effective operation by the owner at his expense. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-341: CITY MANAGER MAY REQUIRE MANHOLE:
When required by the City Manager, the owner of any property serviced by a
building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install a suitable control
manhole, together with such necessary meters and other appurtenances, in the
building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and measurement of the
wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be accessibly and safely located,
and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by the City Manager.
The manhole shall be installed by the owner at his expense and shall be
maintained by him so as to be safe and accessible at all times. (Ord. 257, 12-
14-1981)
17-342: MEASUREMENTS, TESTS AND ANALYSES OF WASTES TO MEET CERTAIN STANDARDS:
All measurements, tests and analyses of the characteristics of waters and
wastes to which reference is made in this Chapter shall be determined in
accordance with the latest edition of "Standard Methods for the Examination of
Water and Wastewater", published by the American Public Health Association, and
shall be determined at the control manhole provided or upon suitable samples
taken at the control manhole. In the event that no special manhole has been
required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream
manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the building sewer is
connected. Sampling shall be carried out by customarily accepted methods to
reflect the effect of constituents upon the sewage works and to determine the
existence of hazards to life, limb and property. The particular analyses
involved will determine whether a twenty four (24) hour composite of all
outfalls of a premises is appropriate or whether a grab sample, or samples,
should be taken. Normally, but not always, BOD and suspended solids analyses
are obtained from twenty four (24) hour composites of all outfalls whereas the
pH is determined from periodic grab samples. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-343: CITY MAY ACCEPT CERTAIN WASTE BY AGREEMENT:
No statement contained in this Chapter shall be construed as preventing any
special agreement or arrangement between the City and any industrial concern
whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by
the City for treatment, subject to payment therefor by the industrial concern
in accordance with the user charge section of this Chapter. (Ord. 257, 12-14-
1981)
17-344: PROTECTION FROM DAMAGE:
No unauthorized person shall maliciously, wilfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or
equipment which is a part of the sewage works. Any person violating this
provision shall be subject to immediate arrest under charge of disorderly
conduct. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-345: POWERS AND AUTHORITY OF INSPECTORS:
   A.   The Plumbing Inspector and other duly authorized employees of the City
bearing proper credentials and identification are permitted to enter all
properties for the purpose of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling
and testing in accordance with the provisions of this Chapter. The Plumbing
Inspector or his representatives have no authority to inquire into any
processes including metallurgical, chemical, oil, refining, ceramic, paper or
other industries beyond that point having a direct bearing on the kind and
source of discharge to the sewers or waterways or facilities for waste
treatment.
   B.   While performing the necessary work on private properties referred to
in subsection A of this Section, the Plumbing Inspector or duly authorized
employees of the City shall observe all safety rules applicable to the premises
established by the company and the company shall be held harmless for injury or
death to the City employees and the City shall indemnify the company against
loss or damage to its property by City employees and against liability claims
and demands for personal injury or property damage asserted against the company
and growing out of the gauging and sampling operation, except as such may be
caused by negligence or failure of the company to maintain safe conditions.
   C.   The Plumbing Inspector and other duly authorized employees of the City
bearing proper credentials and identification are permitted to enter all
private properties through which the City holds a duly negotiated easement for
the purpose of, but not limited to, inspection, observation, measurement,
sampling, repair and maintenance of any portion of the sewage works lying
within the easement. All entry and subsequent work, if any, on the easement
shall be done in full accordance with the terms of the duly negotiated easement
pertaining to the private property involved. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
17-346: PENALTIES:
   A.   Any person found to be violating any provisions of this Chapter except
Section
17-343 of this Chapter shall be served by the City with written notice stating
the nature of the violation and providing a reasonable time limit for the
satisfactory correction thereof. The offender shall, within the period of time
stated in such notice permanently cease all violations.
   B.   Any person who shall continue any violation beyond the time limit
provided for in subsection A of this Section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor,
and on conviction thereof shall be fined as provided in Section
1-108 of this Code.
   C.   Any person violating any of the provisions of this Chapter shall become
liable to the City for any expense, loss or damage occasioned the City by
reason of such violation. (Ord. 257, 12-14-1981)
CHAPTER 4
REFUSE COLLECTION
SECTION:
17-401: Garbage Collection Established
17-402: City To Collect Garbage And Other Refuse
17-403: Approved Containers
17-404: Fees
17-405: Number Of Collections Established
17-406: Garbage Fees Billed With Other Utilities; Penalty For Nonpayment
17-407: Unauthorized Disposal, Hauling Prohibited
17-408: Accumulations Of Garbage And Other Refuse
17-409: Penalty
17-401: GARBAGE COLLECTION ESTABLISHED:
There is hereby established a system for the collection of garbage and trash in
the City. (Prior Code § 9-1)
17-402: CITY TO COLLECT GARBAGE AND OTHER REFUSE:
The City may operate the collection of garbage and trash in the City or it may
contract with any person or firm or organization for the collection of such
garbage and trash in the City. (Prior Code § 9-2)
17-403: APPROVED CONTAINERS:
   A.   The acceptable and approved residential refuse container required by
this chapter shall be a receptacle that is not less than thirty (30) gallons,
but not more than ninety six (96) gallons in volume, capable of holding
impervious material, and is of sturdy construction, with a tight-fitting cover,
equipped with at least two (2) handles properly spaced to facilitate handling.
Trash and refuse contained within such containers shall be bagged within the
receptacles upon collection. Bagged yard waste of a reasonable size for
handling may be placed outside and adjacent to acceptable containers for
collection. 55-gallon drum containers are expressly prohibited.
   B.   Residential refuse containers shall be removed from the curb, and
placed back in their appropriate housing areas, within twenty four (24) hours
after collection. (Ord. 473, 5-14-2018)
17-404: FEES:
   A.   The fees for the services regulated pursuant to this chapter shall be
determined by resolution adopted, and subsequently updated from time to time,
by the City Council, which fees shall be paid by those residents, businesses,
and others using the service.
   B.   For persons living outside the corporate City limits there is hereby
established a permit fee allowing them use of the City dumpsters located at the
City Barn. Said fee shall be equal to that assessed to City residents unless
changed and updated by adoption of a resolution by the City Council. No dumping
shall be permitted on Sundays or holidays. (Ord. 473, 5-14-2018)
17-405: NUMBER OF COLLECTIONS ESTABLISHED:
Trash and garbage shall be hauled a minimum of one time per week for commercial
accounts utilizing a dumpster. If more than one pickup per week is needed,
additional pickups will be provided at an additional fee established by motion
or resolution by the City Council. The Public Works Director, upon approval
from the City Manager, may establish the minimum pick-up requirements for
commercial accounts. Residential customers' trash will be picked up one time
per week. Burning trash and garbage in the City is hereby prohibited. (Ord.
316, 11-14-1994)
17-406: GARBAGE FEES BILLED WITH OTHER UTILITIES; PENALTY FOR NONPAYMENT:
All charges for garbage services shall be paid to the City, and such bill for
such garbage services shall be added to the other utility bills for the
respective residences, businesses and corporations, and failure to pay any
utility bill due the City, including the bill for garbage and trash hauling,
shall subject the delinquent parties to being denied utility services of any
kind by the City, until such payments have been made. All utility bills due the
City from any one customer may each month be compiled into one itemized bill.
(Prior Code § 9-6)
17-407: UNAUTHORIZED DISPOSAL, HAULING PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful and deemed an offense for any person, business, firm or
corporation to dispose or haul garbage, other than herein provided, and any
person failing to use the services of the City in hauling trash and garbage is
deemed guilty of an offense. Any individual caught illegally dumping without a
permit in any trash receptacle as defined herein shall be subject to a penalty
(see section
17-409 of this chapter), subject to the garbage collection services provided by
the City of Prague. (Ord. 448, 9-8-2014)
17-408: ACCUMULATIONS OF GARBAGE AND OTHER REFUSE:
No person shall permit garbage or other refuse to accumulate on premises
occupied by him in such manner that the garbage or other refuse becomes a
hazard to the health or safety of others. Such an accumulation of garbage or
other refuse is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and may be abated as such.
(1983 Code)
17-409: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor, and upon conviction, shall be fined as provided in section
1-108 of this Code. (Prior Code § 9-8)
CHAPTER 5
LANDFILL REGULATIONS
SECTION:
17-501: Short Title
17-502: Designation As Utility (Rep. by Ord. 305-A, 7-26-1993)
17-503: Definitions
17-504: Authorizing Operation And Maintenance
17-505: Fixing Of Use Rates
17-506: Times Of Operation Of Landfill
17-507: Providing For Rules And Regulations
17-508: Violation Prohibited
17-509: Declaration Of City Property
17-510: Unauthorized Dumping Of Trash Declared A Nuisance And Prohibited
17-511: Presumption Of Illegal Dumping
17-512: Penalties
17-501: SHORT TITLE:
This Chapter may hereinafter be known as THE LANDFILL ORDINANCE. (Ord. 279, 9-
8-1985)
17-502: DESIGNATION AS UTILITY:
(Rep. by Ord. 305-A, 7-26-1993)
17-503: DEFINITIONS:
As used herein:
OTHER TRASH: All other types of solid waste whatsoever regardless of its
content or makeup.
TRASH: Such solid waste as is defined under Class 6 of the statutes of the
State of Oklahoma or other types of solid waste permitted to be placed in the
landfill by the laws of the State of Oklahoma. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
17-504: AUTHORIZING OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE:
The Prague Public Works Authority is hereby authorized to operate and maintain
the landfill in such form and fashion as will comply with all of the laws of
the State and the Federal Government thereto pertaining, and that the Prague
Public Works Authority shall be vested with all authority necessary to operate
and maintain the landfill in an orderly and lawful fashion. (Ord. 279, 9-8-
1985)
17-505: FIXING OF USE RATES:
The manager of the Prague Public Works Authority, with the advice and consent
of the trustees of the Prague Public Works Authority, shall fix such rates for
the dumping of trash in the landfill as he may deem reasonable to defray the
expense thereof and he is authorized from time to time to change or adjust the
same, subject to the trustees' advice and consent, but once fixed the same
shall remain in full force and effect for a period of not less than thirty (30)
days and such rates shall be kept and published in the office of the City
Clerk. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
17-506: TIMES OF OPERATION OF LANDFILL:
The manager of the Prague Public Works Authority, subject to the advice and
consent of the trustees of the Authority, shall prepare and publish a schedule
of days of the week that the landfill will be open, as well as the hours of
opening and closing thereon. The manager will cause a schedule of such openings
and closings to be posted at the City Hall and a copy thereof shall be kept and
maintained by the City Clerk for public reference. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
17-507: PROVIDING FOR RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The manager of the Prague Public Works Authority shall develop and maintain a
comprehensive set of rules and regulations pertaining to the use and
maintenance of the landfill in accordance with the laws, rules and regulations
of the State as well as the United States Government, and such laws, rules and
regulations of the State or United States which are applicable, as well as
those developed by the manager, and as may be subsequently amended, are hereby
adopted as part of this Chapter by reference thereto as though fully set out
herein. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
17-508: VIOLATION PROHIBITED:
Violation of any law, rules and regulations as are applicable to the operation
of the landfill is hereby prohibited and violation thereof shall constitute a
misdemeanor under the ordinances of the City. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
17-509: DECLARATION OF CITY PROPERTY:
The landfill is declared to be part of the City including the rights of way
immediately abutting thereto and the same shall be subject to all applicable
ordinances of the City. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
17-510: UNAUTHORIZED DUMPING OF TRASH DECLARED A NUISANCE AND PROHIBITED:
The dumping of "trash", as defined herein, garbage or other materials or
substances of whatever kind or description on the landfill or the ditches and
roadway abutting thereto is a public nuisance and is strictly prohibited,
provided however, that nothing herein shall be interpreted as preventing the
disposal of lawful "trash", as defined herein, at such locations specifically
provided for the same as designated by the manager of the Prague Public Works
Authority, or his agents, servants and employees, on a day-to-day basis. The
dumping of trash in any other location than that designated shall be deemed a
violation of this Section. Any person found dumping such trash in other than a
designated location shall upon conviction be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor as
herein provided. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
17-511: PRESUMPTION OF ILLEGAL DUMPING:
Trash which is dumped or abandoned on the landfill or the ditches or rights of
way immediately abutting thereto which can be identified through writings,
postal addresses or other items containing markings identifying the owner or
recipient thereof shall constitute a rebuttable presumption of the ownership
thereof in the court of the City and once established the burden of rebutting
the presumption shall rest on the person identified thereby. The dumping of
trash by other than the owners thereof shall be no defense to a violation of
this Section. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
17-512: PENALTIES:
Each and every violation of any of the provisions contained in this Chapter is
an offense against the City and upon conviction of such offense the violator or
violators will be punished as provided in Section
1-108 of this Code. (Ord. 279, 9-8-1985)
CHAPTER 6
ELECTRIC SERVICE
SECTION:
17-601: Control Of Electric System
17-602: Inspection
17-603: Billing And Payment
17-604: Interruption Of Service
17-605: Resumption Of Electricity Authorized
17-606: Application For Electrical Service; Deposit
17-607: Tampering With Electric Meters
17-608: Service Line Installation
17-609: Connection To Electric Supply Required
17-610: Testing Electric Meters
17-611: Penalties
17-601: CONTROL OF ELECTRIC SYSTEM:
The electric power and distribution system of the city of Prague shall be under
the control of the city manager, who shall be governed by the rules and
regulations set forth herein, and he shall have authority to approve, or
disapprove, all accounts for expenditures in this department and no accounts or
claims shall be paid until approved by the city manager. All electric current
shall be used through meters at rates set by resolution adopted by the public
works authority. The manager shall provide regulations and fees for extra
services relating to nonpayment of bills, disconnect and reconnect service,
request for abnormal services, returned checks, and any other nonroutine
services. Meters shall be read by the city, and all readings shall be turned
over to the utility clerk for billing. Electrical lines used for distribution
of electricity and the meters attached thereto are the property of the city of
Prague and shall be controlled by it, and must be accessible as determined by
the city of Prague at all times for the purposes of reading and servicing.
(Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
17-602: INSPECTION:
   A.   The wiring of all public buildings shall be done in accordance with
this code or any other ordinances of the city, and no connections shall be made
until such wiring has been inspected and approved by the city electrical
inspector. (Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
   B.   1. Any vacant property seeking electric service connection within the
service area of the Prague public works authority shall be subject to an
inspection of all electrical systems by the city of Prague prior to connection.
For purposes of this subsection B only, a vacant property shall be any property
that has been without utility service for a period of ninety (90) days or
greater.
      2.   The city of Prague may deny connection to electrical service if the
condition of the vacant property's electrical system(s) poses a threat to the
health, safety and welfare of the inhabitants of the structure or to the
community.
      3.   In the event that the city of Prague declines to provide electric
service as outlined in subsection B2 of this section, the city of Prague will
provide the property owner with a list of necessary repairs that if completed,
would enable the property to be connected to electrical service. (Ord. 434, 8-
13-2012)
17-603: BILLING AND PAYMENT:
The charges for electric current sold to customers shall become due and payable
in full at least once each month. Electric meters must be accessible to the
city of Prague personnel for reading and service. If it is determined that the
meter is inaccessible, the city manager shall have the authority to require the
customer, at customer's expense, to relocate the service entry point to an
accessible location as determined by the city manager or his designee. Said
installation shall be in accordance with all provisions of the city's
electrical codes. Charges are due and payable upon receipt of a bill. If
payment is not made by the due date, a late payment charge of ten percent (10%)
of the total bill due and owing will be added. If payment has not been received
by the twenty fifth of the month, or a deferred payment arrangement made, the
service will be discontinued for nonpayment. No other notice of disconnection
of service will be required. This will apply regardless of whether or not the
same parties occupy the premises where the electricity was used. Should service
be discontinued because of nonpayment as herein provided, service will not
again be provided for the person who originally made the application, in the
same house or premises, until all arrears are paid together with the fee for
disconnecting and connecting service lines. An additional deposit amount to be
determined by the City Manager may also be required prior to restoration of
service. (Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
17-604: INTERRUPTION OF SERVICE:
No additions, changes, or alterations in the service lines shall be made by the
consumer except that same shall be done with the approval of the City. It shall
be the contract between the City and each and every consumer that no claim be
made or allowed against the City for damages caused by or because of the
breaking or faulting of feeder or service lines, either underground or
overhead. No claim shall be allowed for single phasing on 3-phase equipment or
for damage to voltage sensitive electronic equipment. The City reserves the
right to cut off current anywhere or the entire system for repairs, or in case
of emergency, storm, fire, etc. (Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
17-605: RESUMPTION OF ELECTRICITY AUTHORIZED:
No person or persons, from whose premises current has been cut off for any
reason shall turn the current on, or cause the same to be turned on, without
authority from the City Manager or his designee. In no event shall electric
service be supplied through any meter other than the meter assigned to that
account by the City of Prague. The conditions of this chapter shall be deemed a
contract between each patron and the City of Prague and the City reserves the
right to amend, alter, or change the terms of this chapter as often as deemed
expedient and for the welfare of the citizens of Prague. (Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
17-606: APPLICATION FOR ELECTRICAL SERVICE; DEPOSIT:
Any person desiring the use of electric current shall make application in
writing to the utility office of the City of Prague, which application shall
set out the location of the property, the purpose for which the current is to
be used, the identity and mailing address of the customer responsible for
payment. Such application must be signed by the customer or his agent holding a
power of attorney, and shall be approved by the City. Such application must be
accompanied by a deposit in an amount set by the Public Works Authority. If in
the opinion of the City Manager additional security is necessary to insure the
City against loss, then the applicant must make a deposit of the amount
sufficient to insure the payment of a current monthly bill. When the contract
for electric service is terminated and the City has disconnected such service,
the deposit shall be applied to the final bill and any excess funds returned to
him after all bills and fees are paid. (Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
17-607: TAMPERING WITH ELECTRIC METERS:
No person except those persons authorized by the City Manager shall turn on any
electric meter after that meter has been turned off by the City; nor shall any
person except those authorized to do so by the City Manager, alter, interfere,
meddle with, wire around, or use jumpers on any electric meter belonging to the
City of Prague, except in cases of emergency. Any such emergency action must be
reported to the City of Prague no later than ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. on the
first working day following the emergency action. The City Manager shall
determine the policy to be used by City personnel in investigation of suspected
unauthorized electrical connection. Each meter so altered shall be deemed a
separate offense, and each day such violation continues shall be a separate
offense. (Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
17-608: SERVICE LINE INSTALLATION:
The electrical service line or service lateral, as defined by the National
Electrical Code, from the secondary or line in the utility easement, to the
meter loop on the structure, shall be installed by the City of Prague or by
someone duly authorized by the City. Charges for the installation of the
electrical service line shall be based off of the actual costs of materials and
labor associated with the installation, by the City. It is unlawful for any
person, firm or corporation other than the City of Prague, to install any
electrical service or service laterals as provided in this section unless the
person, firm or corporation has been authorized in writing by the City Manager
or his designee to perform such work. (Ord. 462, 1-11-2016)
17-609: CONNECTION TO ELECTRIC SUPPLY REQUIRED:
   A.   Required: All commercial and industrial buildings or properties to be
constructed, added to, or altered within the City of Prague, and all
residential buildings, uses, or properties shall connect with the electrical
supply of the City of Prague.
   B.   Exception To Connection Requirement: The provisions of this section
shall not apply to:
      1.   A structure constructed outside a platted subdivision where in the
opinion of the City it is not economically feasible to connect the structure
with the Prague electric system.
      2.   All land uses permitted where the subdivision or structure was
constructed in a previously platted area served by an electrical system other
than that of the City of Prague. (Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
17-610: TESTING ELECTRIC METERS:
In the event any user shall question the accuracy of any meter and if he shall
want the meter tested, such user shall make his requests with the City Clerk
and shall make a deposit in an amount set by the City Manager with said Clerk.
An employee of the City designated by the City Manager shall then remove the
meter and submit for testing. If the meter shows an error in favor of the user
in excess of two percent (2%) the user shall be credited with such an amount as
the Manager shall decide is right, just and equitable, taking into
consideration the amount of electricity that was probably consumed by such user
during the time under dispute. In such case the deposit left by him shall be
returned to him; however if the test should show that the meter did not vary
more than two percent (2%), as above stated, then the deposit shall be retained
by the Clerk to pay the expense of removing, testing and replacing the meter.
(Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
17-611: PENALTIES:
Any person, firm, or corporation who violates any provision of this chapter
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction, shall be fined as
provided in section
1-108 of this Code. (Ord. 409, 12-8-2008)
PART 18
MEDICAL MARIJUANA REGULATIONS

18-101: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and terms, when used in this Chapter and Article, shall
have the following meaning, unless the context clearly indicates otherwise, and
in accordance with OAC 310: 681-1-4.
APPLICANT: The natural person or entity in whose name a license would be
           issued.

COMMERCIAL
ESTABLISHMENT     An individual or entity licensed under this Part and/or Chapter as a medical
("ESTABLISHMENT") marijuana dispensary, grower, processor, or researcher.
OR COMMERCIAL
LICENSEE:

LICENSE:          researcher.
